  1830  +**Notes & Considerations (as a Front-End Engineer):**
  1831  +
  1832  +*   **Placeholder Image:** I've included a placeholder image (`placeholder-hero-image.jpg`).  We *need* to identify the actual content to select a proper image.  Let’s prioritize a high-quality, relevant image that immediately communicates our value proposition.
  1833  +*   **Responsiveness:**  I’ve set the `img` width to `100%` and `height: auto` to ensure it scales properly.  For full responsiveness, we’ll need to use media queries in the CSS to adjust the image size and layout at different screen sizes (mobile, tablet, desktop).
  1834  +*   **Accessibility:** I've included an `alt` attribute on the `img` tag for accessibility.  It’s *crucial* to provide descriptive alt text for all images.
  1835  +*   **Performance:**  Optimizing the image file size is important for performance.  We should use appropriate image formats (e.g., WebP if supported) and consider image compression.
  1836  +*   **Next Steps:** I think the next critical step is to solidify the content for the hero section and then start implementing the media query adjustments for the hero section.  Let's discuss the content and I’ll start working on the responsive media queries.
  1837  +

  1981  +
  1982  +**4. Content for the Hero Section:**
  1983  +
  1984  +Let’s go with this content for the hero section. It aligns with a modern, tech-focused brand:
  1985  +
  1986  +*   **Headline:** “Revolutionizing [Industry Name] with Innovative Solutions” (Montserrat, Bold)
  1987  +*   **Subheadline:** “We deliver powerful, user-friendly platforms designed to drive growth and efficiency.” (Open Sans, Regular)
  1988  +*   **Brief Description:** “[Company Name] is a leading provider of [brief description of services/products]. We’re dedicated to helping businesses like yours achieve their goals through cutting-edge technology and exceptional customer support.”
  1989  +*   **Call to Action Button:** “Get Started Today” (Coral, White Text)
  1990  +
  1991  +**5. Next Steps & Considerations:**
  1992  +
  1993  +*   **Hero Image Content:** *Critical:* We need to quickly determine the key content of the hero section to select an appropriate image.  Considering the hero content above, let’s aim for an image depicting people using our platform successfully, or a sleek, abstract representation of innovation.
  1994  +*   **Content Hierarchy:** Let’s discuss the most important information to display on the page and how to prioritize it visually (e.g., headings, subheadings, key facts).
  1995  +*   **Mobile Responsiveness:** Remember to keep in mind how this design will translate to different screen sizes.
  1996  +*   **Image Optimization:** The Front-End Engineer should prioritize image optimization (WebP if possible) and ensure the alt text is descriptive.
  1997  +
  1998  +**6. Front-End Engineer Notes (Updated):**
  1999  +
  2000  +*   **Responsiveness:** Let’s prioritize the mobile responsiveness *first*. Given the provided HTML and CSS, starting with mobile will ensure the core layout and typography are appropriately scaled. We can then build up to the desktop layout.
  2001  +*   **Image Optimization:** As stated above, optimizing the image file size is crucial. Let’s research WebP support and explore image compression techniques.
  2002  +*   **Accessibility:**  The `alt` attribute on the `img` tag is a great start.  We’ll need to refine the description further as we choose the final image.
  2003  +
  2004  +**What content should we put in the hero section, and do we want to prioritize the mobile responsiveness now, or prioritize the desktop layout first?** We’re going to start with the mobile responsiveness. Let's focus on building a solid mobile foundation – the responsive implementation is the next critical task.

  2225  +Designer contributing (streaming):
  2226  +Okay, fantastic! I’m really liking the direction we're taking – the teal and coral combination feels very modern and approachable. Focusing on mobile-first is brilliant; it's the smartest way to build a solid foundation.
  2227  +
  2228  +Given the hero content we've established ("Revolutionizing [Industry Name] with Innovative Solutions…”) and the overall brand vibe, I'd like to suggest a slightly more dynamic image for the hero section. Instead of just depicting users *using* the platform, let’s go for something that subtly represents innovation and forward-thinking.
  2229  +
  2230  +**Specifically, I'd propose an image of a stylized, interconnected network of nodes glowing with a subtle teal light.** It wouldn’t be literal, but rather an abstract representation of data flow, connection, and technological advancement. The nodes could have a slight gradient – starting with a lighter teal and fading to a darker teal – to add depth. This aligns with the "revolutionizing" message and visually communicates the ‘innovative solutions’ aspect.
  2231  +
  2232  +**Regarding typography –** while Montserrat for the headings is a good choice, for the subheadline (“We deliver…”) I’d suggest a slightly lighter weight to give it a bit more breathing room and enhance readability. Perhaps Montserrat Light.
  2233  +
  2234  +**For the hero section layout itself –** I think a slightly wider hero section (around 60% width) would allow the image to dominate and draw the eye effectively.  Let's maintain that generous whitespace (30px) between the image and the text.
  2235  +
  2236  +**Let's double-check the color contrast too.** With the coral CTA button, ensuring the text color has *significant* contrast against the off-white background is absolutely key to accessibility.
  2237  +
  2238  +**To summarize, my recommendations are:**
  2239  +
  2240  +*   **Hero Image:** Stylized, abstract representation of interconnected nodes (teal gradient).
  2241  +*   **Subheadline Typography:** Montserrat Light.
  2242  +*   **Layout:** Slightly wider hero section (60% width).
  2243  +
  2244  +**I'm firmly in favor of prioritizing mobile responsiveness.** Let’s build that solid foundation first – that’s going to make the whole process significantly smoother.  Let's continue to keep accessibility top of mind throughout the development!
  2245  +
  2246  +Do we have any concerns about this direction? Would anyone like to explore alternative image concepts – perhaps focusing on a single, elegant device within a futuristic setting?

  2667  +--- Engineer is thinking ---
  2668  +System Prompt:
  2669  +**Objective:** To collaboratively design a simple, responsive web page, prioritizing a clean, modern aesthetic with a strong focus on readability and user engagement.
  2670  +
  2671  +**Current Focus:** Mobile-First Responsive Design. We are currently prioritizing the creation of a solid mobile foundation for the web page.
  2672  +
  2673  +**Key Design Principles:**
  2674  +
  2675  +*   **Clean & Modern:** Emphasize whitespace, clear typography, and a minimalist approach.
  2676  +*   **Readability:** Prioritize font choices and color contrast to ensure optimal readability.
  2677  +*   **Responsive Design:**  Maintain a mobile-first approach, iteratively expanding the design to accommodate larger screen sizes.
  2678  +
  2679  +**Action Items & Reminders:**
  2680  +
  2681  +*   **Hero Image Content:** *Critical:* The team *must* immediately determine the specific content for the hero section image.  Let's aim for an image depicting people using our platform successfully, or a sleek, abstract representation of innovation.  Let’s establish a clear requirement for the image – one sentence describing the image’s purpose.
  2682  +*   **Content Hierarchy:**  Maintain a focus on clear content hierarchy – headings, subheadings, and key facts should be clearly distinguished.
  2683  +*   **Accessibility:**  Ensure appropriate `alt` text is provided for all images and consider accessibility best practices throughout the design.  (Specifically, let's ensure sufficient color contrast between text and background colors.)
  2684  +*   **Image Optimization:**  The Front-End Engineer is responsible for researching and implementing WebP support and exploring image compression techniques.
  2685  +
  2686  +**Process Reminders:**
  2687  +
  2688  +*   **Decision-Making:**  Let's strive for quick decisions, especially regarding the hero image content and image selection.
  2689  +*   **Iteration:**  This is an iterative process. We'll refine the design based on feedback and testing.
  2690  +*   **Communication:**  Let’s keep the conversation focused and efficient.
  2691  +
  2692  +**Open Questions:**
  2693  +
  2694  +*   Regarding the hero image, what is the *primary* goal of the image (e.g., illustrate a user benefit, represent the brand, provide context)?
  2695  +*   Do we want to establish a target screen size for initial mobile responsiveness (e.g., iPhone 14, Android Latest)?

  3049  +
  3050  +**My Questions for the Team:**
  3051  +
  3052  +1.  **Primary Goal of the Hero Image:**  Before I even look at potential image assets, I need to understand the *purpose* of this image.  Is it meant to *immediately* communicate a key benefit of our platform (e.g., "A team collaboratively using our platform to streamline their workflow")?  Is it to establish brand recognition (a sleek, modern representation of innovation, perhaps)? Or is it to provide contextual information about our product?  Knowing the primary goal will dramatically influence my approach to selection and potentially even the image editing process itself.
  3053  +
  3054  +2.  **Target Mobile Screen Size:** Let's establish a target screen size for our initial mobile responsiveness.  iPhone 14 is a good starting point for a current-generation device, but is there a specific device we’re particularly focused on reaching?  Knowing the target size will allow me to begin thinking about media queries and the responsive grid system.
  3055  +
  3056  +**My Immediate Tasks (Based on the Current Focus):**
  3057  +
  3058  +*   **WebP Research:** I’ll immediately start researching WebP support across modern browsers. I’ll look into libraries and techniques for seamless integration.  I’ll also begin investigating effective image compression techniques – lossless and lossy – to ensure optimal image sizes without sacrificing visual quality.
  3059  +*   **Responsive Grid Framework:** I’ll be familiarizing myself with a responsive grid framework (likely CSS Grid or Flexbox) to create the underlying structure for the page, ensuring it adapts gracefully to different screen sizes.
  3060  +*   **Accessibility Baseline:** I'll start outlining a basic accessibility plan. This will include using semantic HTML elements, providing descriptive `alt` text for *all* images (which will be absolutely essential once we have a selection), and ensuring sufficient color contrast between text and background colors.  I'll use a color contrast checker tool to verify this.
  3061  +
  3062  +
  3063  +**Let's get this done efficiently. Once we have a defined understanding of the hero image’s purpose and target screen size, I can start exploring suitable image assets and begin implementing the responsive grid framework.**

  3410  +New Contribution:
  3411  +Okay, let’s get to work. As the Front-End Engineer, my priority is building a solid, performant, and accessible foundation for this web page, keeping the design principles firmly in mind. 
  3412  +
  3413  +First, regarding the hero image – that’s *critical* as you’ve rightly pointed out. I need specifics to start thinking about the implementation.
  3414  +
  3415  +**My Questions for the Team:**
  3416  +
  3417  +1.  **Primary Goal of the Hero Image:**  Before I even look at potential image assets, I need to understand the *purpose* of this image.  Is it meant to *immediately* communicate a key benefit of our platform (e.g., "A team collaboratively using our platform to streamline their workflow")?  Is it to establish brand recognition (a sleek, modern representation of innovation, perhaps)? Or is it to provide contextual information about our product?  Knowing the primary goal will dramatically influence my approach to selection and potentially even the image editing process itself.
  3418  +
  3419  +2.  **Target Mobile Screen Size:** Let's establish a target screen size for our initial mobile responsiveness.  iPhone 14 is a good starting point for a current-generation device, but is there a specific device we’re particularly focused on reaching?  Knowing the target size will allow me to begin thinking about media queries and the responsive grid system.
  3420  +
  3421  +**My Immediate Tasks (Based on the Current Focus):**

  3626  +Welcome to aichat 0.29.0
  3627  +Type ".help" for additional help.
  3628  +> what is the sshfs option for read caching?
  3629  +The primary `sshfs` option that enables read caching (caching of file data, attributes, and directory entries) is:
  3630  +
  3631  +*   `-o cache=yes`
  3632  +
  3633  +While `cache=yes` enables the caching mechanism for reads, the *behavior* and *freshness* of the cache are controlled by timeout options:
  3634  +
  3635  +*   `-o cache_timeout=N`: This is a general timeout (in seconds) that applies to *all* cached data (attributes, directory entries, and file data). The client will trust its cached information for `N` seconds before re-querying the server.
  3636  +*   `-o entry_timeout=N`: Specifically controls the timeout (in seconds) for directory entries (filenames, inode numbers).
  3637  +*   `-o attribute_timeout=N`: Specifically controls the timeout (in seconds) for file attributes (size, permissions, timestamps, etc.).
  3638  +
  3639  +**How it works:**
  3640  +
  3641  +*   When you use `-o cache=yes`, `sshfs` will store copies of file data blocks, directory listings, and file attributes locally.
  3642  +*   When an application requests data or information, `sshfs` first checks its local cache.
  3643  +*   If the data is in the cache and hasn't expired according to the timeout settings (`cache_timeout`, `entry_timeout`, `attribute_timeout`), `sshfs` serves it directly from the cache, which is much faster than fetching it from the remote server.
  3644  +*   If the data is not in the cache or has expired, `sshfs` fetches it from the server and stores it in the cache for future use (until the timeout expires).
  3645  +
  3646  +**Important Considerations:**
  3647  +
  3648  +*   `cache=yes` is often the **default** behavior in recent `sshfs` versions, but explicitly specifying it is harmless and can be useful for clarity or compatibility with older versions.
  3649  +*   Longer timeout values (higher `N`) improve read performance by reducing server requests but increase the risk of using **stale data** if the remote files change frequently.
  3650  +*   Shorter timeout values reduce the risk of stale data but decrease performance due to more frequent server requests.
  3651  +*   If you need to ensure you *always* get the latest data from the server, you would use `-o cache=no`, but this significantly impacts performance.
  3652  +
  3653  +**In summary:** Use `-o cache=yes` to enable read caching, and adjust `-o cache_timeout`, `-o entry_timeout`, and `-o attribute_timeout` to control how long the cached data is considered valid.
  3654  +
  3655  +>

  3700  +import ollama  # Keep the import for completeness, though we'll simulate its use
  3701  +import re
  3702  +from colorama import Fore, Style, init
  3703  +
  3704  +init(autoreset=True)
  3705  +
  3706  +AGENT_COLORS = {
  3707  +    "Designer": Fore.CYAN,
  3708  +    "Engineer": Fore.GREEN,
  3709  +    "PromptDev": Fore.MAGENTA
  3710  +}
  3711  +BANNER_COLOR = Fore.LIGHTYELLOW_EX
  3712  +LABEL_COLOR = Fore.YELLOW
  3713  +ROUND_COLOR = Fore.RED
  3714  +AGENT_ROUND_COLOR = Fore.LIGHTRED_EX
  3715  +CANVAS_ROUND_COLOR = Fore.LIGHTMAGENTA_EX
  3716  +
  3717  +class Agent:
  3718  +    """Represents an agent with a name, model, and persona."""
  3719  +    def __init__(self, name, model, persona):
  3720  +        self.name = name
  3721  +        self.model = model
  3722  +        self.persona = persona
  3723  +
  3724  +    def generate_response(self, system_prompt, session_prompt, canvas):
  3725  +        color = AGENT_COLORS.get(self.name, Fore.WHITE)
  3726  +        #print(f"\n{color}--- {self.name} is thinking ---{Style.RESET_ALL}")
  3727  +        print(f"\n\n{AGENT_ROUND_COLOR}--- {self.name} is thinking ---{Style.RESET_ALL}")
  3728  +        # Construct the messages list for ollama.chat
  3729  +        messages = [
  3730  +            {"role": "system", "content": f"System Prompt:\n{system_prompt}\n\n"},
  3731  +            {"role": "user", "content": f"Session Prompt:\n{session_prompt}\n\n"},
  3732  +            {"role": "user", "content": f"Shared Canvas:\n{canvas}\n\n"},
  3733  +            {"role": "user", "content": f"Your persona: {self.persona}\n"}
  3734  +        ]
  3735  +
  3736  +        for msg in messages:
  3737  +            label, _, content = msg['content'].partition(':')
  3738  +            print(f"{LABEL_COLOR}{label}:{Style.RESET_ALL}{content}")
  3739  +            print("  ...." * 10)
  3740  +
  3741  +
  3742  +        full_response = ""
  3743  +        print(f"\n{color}{self.name} contributing (streaming):{Style.RESET_ALL}")
  3744  +
  3745  +        # Use ollama.chat in stream mode
  3746  +        stream = ollama.chat(
  3747  +            model=self.model,
  3748  +            messages=messages,
  3749  +            stream=True,
  3750  +        )
  3751  +
  3752  +        # Process the streamed response
  3753  +        for chunk in stream:
  3754  +            if chunk['message']['content'] is not None:
  3755  +                content = chunk['message']['content']
  3756  +                print(content, end='', flush=True) # Print as it arrives
  3757  +                full_response += content
  3758  +
  3759  +        print(f"\n{'-'*60}\n")
  3760  +        print(f"--- {self.name} finished thinking ---\n")
  3761  +
  3762  +        return full_response.strip()
  3763  +
  3764  +def extract_revised_system_prompt(contribution):
  3765  +    """
  3766  +    Extracts the revised system prompt from PromptDev's contribution.
  3767  +    Looks for a heading or marker and returns the following section.
  3768  +    """
  3769  +    # Try to find the heading and capture all lines until a triple newline or end of string
  3770  +    match = re.search(
  3771  +        r"\*?\*?.*System Prompt.*\*?\*?\s*\n+([\s\S]*?)(?:\n\-{3,}\n|\n{3,}|\Z)", contribution
  3772  +    )
  3773  +    if match:
  3774  +        # Return the extracted prompt, stripped of leading/trailing whitespace
  3775  +        return match.group(1).strip()
  3776  +    else:
  3777  +        # Fallback: return the whole contribution (as before)
  3778  +        return contribution.strip()
  3779  +
  3780  +
  3781  +def extract_updated_canvas(update):
  3782  +    """
  3783  +    Extracts the updated canvas.
  3784  +    """
  3785  +    # Try to find the heading and capture all lines until a triple newline or end of string
  3786  +    match = re.search(
  3787  +        r"\*?\*?.*Canvas.*\*?\*?\s*\n+([\s\S]*?)(?:\n\-{3,}\n|\n{3,}|\Z)", update
  3788  +    )
  3789  +    if match:
  3790  +        # Return the extracted prompt, stripped of leading/trailing whitespace
  3791  +        return match.group(1).strip()
  3792  +    else:
  3793  +        # Fallback: return the whole contribution (as before)
  3794  +        return update.strip()
  3795  +
  3796  +
  3797  +def aggregate_contribution(session_prompt, canvas, contribution):
  3798  +    """
  3799  +    Uses ollama to summarize or merge the new contribution into the shared canvas.
  3800  +    """
  3801  +    print(f"\n\n{CANVAS_ROUND_COLOR}--- --- Updating Canvas --- ---{Style.RESET_ALL}")
  3802  +    prompt = (
  3803  +        "You are a collaborative assistant. Given the current shared canvas and a new contribution, "
  3804  +        "integrate the new contribution into the canvas, preserving important details and ensuring coherence. "
  3805  +        "Do not remove existing valuable content. Return the updated canvas."
  3806  +    )
  3807  +    messages = [
  3808  +        {"role": "system", "content": prompt},
  3809  +        {"role": "user", "content": f"Current Canvas:\n{canvas}\n"},
  3810  +        {"role": "user", "content": f"New Contribution:\n{contribution}\n"}
  3811  +    ]
  3812  +    print(f"\n{Fore.BLUE}Current Canvas:{Style.RESET_ALL}\n{canvas}\n")
  3813  +    print(f"\n{Fore.MAGENTA}New Contribution:{Style.RESET_ALL}\n{contribution}\n")
  3814  +    response = ollama.chat(
  3815  +        model=MODEL,
  3816  +        messages=messages,
  3817  +        stream=False,
  3818  +    )
  3819  +    updated_canvas = extract_updated_canvas(response['message']['content'].strip())
  3820  +    print(f"{Fore.GREEN}Updated Canvas:{Style.RESET_ALL}\n{updated_canvas}\n\n\n\n")
  3821  +    return updated_canvas
  3822  +
  3823  +
  3824  +# Model and Agents
  3825  +MODEL = 'gemma3:4b'  # Placeholder model name
  3826  +designer = Agent(
  3827  +    name="Designer",

  3829  +    persona="Creative Web Designer: Focus on visual aesthetics, user experience, and layout. Suggest color schemes, typography, and design elements."
  3830  +)
  3831  +engineer = Agent(
  3832  +    name="Engineer",
  3833  +    model=MODEL,
  3834  +    persona="Front-End Engineer: Implement designs using HTML, CSS, and JavaScript. Ensure responsiveness, accessibility, and performance."

  3836  +prompt_dev = Agent(
  3837  +    name="PromptDev",
  3838  +    model=MODEL,

  3840  +)
  3841  +

  3843  +

  3847  +    "This is a collaborative multi-agent design session. Each agent will add to or modify the shared canvas below. "
  3848  +    "PromptDev will update the system prompt as needed to keep the team aligned."
  3849  +)

  3855  +print(f"{LABEL_COLOR}Initial Session Prompt:{Style.RESET_ALL}\n{session_prompt}\n")

  3861  +    for agent in agents:
  3862  +        contribution = agent.generate_response(system_prompt, session_prompt, canvas)
  3863  +        if agent.name == "PromptDev":
  3864  +            #print("PromptDev is updating the system prompt...")
  3865  +            system_prompt = extract_revised_system_prompt(contribution)
  3866  +            #canvas = ""  # Optionally clear canvas after prompt update
  3867  +        else:
  3868  +            #canvas += f"{contribution}\n\n\n\n"
  3869  +            canvas = aggregate_contribution(session_prompt, canvas, contribution)
  3870  +    #print("\nCurrent Shared Canvas:\n" + canvas)
  3871  +    #print("Current System Prompt:\n" + system_prompt)
  3872  +    print("-" * 40)
  3873  +

  3875  +print("\nFinal Shared Canvas:\n" + canvas)
  3876  +print("\nFinal System Prompt:\n" + system_prompt)

  5205  +Okay, let’s get this started. Given the initial design choices – the color scheme, typography, and overall approach – I'm seeing a solid foundation for a clean and modern website. My immediate focus will be on ensuring we can translate this into a responsive and accessible design.
  5206  +
  5207  +**Initial Thoughts & Questions (as a Front-End Engineer):**
  5208  +
  5209  +1.  **Responsiveness:** The three-column layout is a good starting point, but we need to consider how this will adapt across different screen sizes. We'll definitely need to use media queries to adjust column widths and potentially stack content vertically on smaller screens. Let’s think about breakpoints – where do we want the layout to shift?
  5210  +
  5211  +2.  **Accessibility:**  I’m noting the use of color – we need to ensure sufficient contrast ratios between text and background colors to meet WCAG guidelines.  Also, we should be mindful of semantic HTML and ARIA attributes to improve accessibility for users with disabilities.
  5212  +
  5213  +3.  **Font Loading:** Poppins and Open Sans are both relatively common fonts. We’ll want to optimize font loading to avoid slow initial render times. Techniques like preloading fonts or using web fonts that are served efficiently would be important.
  5214  +
  5215  +4.  **Regarding the Next Steps:**  I’m leaning towards creating some basic wireframes *before* diving into detailed elements. Starting with a low-fidelity representation will help us quickly iterate on the layout and ensure it’s effective across different screen sizes.
  5216  +
  5217  +**Specific Questions for the Team:**
  5218  +
  5219  +*   **Icon Style:** You mentioned exploring outlined or filled icons. Could we create a quick mock-up of both styles to see which feels more aligned with the “Coastal Calm” concept?
  5220  +*   **Call to Action Buttons:** What color should the call to action buttons be?  The primary color (#66B2FF) feels like a good option, but we should confirm this aligns with the overall brand.

  7564  +For this web page, I’m envisioning a clean, modern, and inviting aesthetic. My initial thoughts are:
  7565  +
  7566  +**Color Scheme:**  I'm leaning towards a **cool-toned palette** with a primary accent color of **teal (#008080)**. Teal evokes feelings of calmness, trustworthiness, and innovation - great for a modern website.  We can use a neutral background – probably a light **gray (#F5F5F5)** – to let the teal and other colors pop.  We could incorporate a secondary accent color of **burnt orange (#CC6633)** sparingly for call-to-action buttons or highlights.
  7567  +
  7568  +**Typography:**
  7569  +*   **Headings:**  I’d suggest a modern, slightly rounded sans-serif font like **Poppins** or **Nunito Sans**.  Something readable and friendly without feeling overly rigid.
  7570  +*   **Body Text:** A classic, highly readable font like **Roboto** or **Open Sans** would work well for the main content.
  7571  +
  7572  +**Design Elements:**
  7573  +
  7574  +*   **Imagery:** High-quality, lifestyle photography is key. Images that feel authentic and relatable will resonate with users. Let's aim for a predominantly bright, airy feel.
  7575  +*   **Spacing:** Generous whitespace is *essential* for a clean, uncluttered look and excellent readability.
  7576  +*   **Call-to-Action Buttons:**  Rounded, teal buttons with a subtle shadow effect will draw the eye and create a clear pathway for the user.
  7577  +*   **Subtle Animations:**  Consider very subtle hover effects or transitions to add a touch of polish and delight without being distracting.
  7578  +
  7579  +**Initial Layout Thoughts:** A classic two-column layout with a larger hero image on the left and content on the right would be a good starting point.
  7580  +

  8767  +I agree completely with the strategy of replacing magic numbers with constants. It’s a fundamental best practice and directly addresses a significant risk for future maintainability. The "Configuration Constants" file is a good idea – keeping these values centralized is crucial.
  8768  +
  8769  +However, I have a question regarding the documentation template you’ve proposed. While the `@name`, `@type`, and `@description` fields are useful, I'm concerned that simply stating the description *within* the Javadoc-style comment might not be sufficient. We need to ensure that the *reason* for the constant's existence is clearly understood. I suggest adding a field specifically for “Context” – a brief explanation of *why* this constant is used in the broader context of the discount calculation. 
  8770  +
  8771  +For example, instead of just “Default discount percentage for new customers,” we need something like: "Default discount percentage for new customers as part of our onboarding incentive program." This provides more context for someone unfamiliar with the specific discount rules.
  8772  +
  8773  +Also, regarding tracking the source – I concur that we need a documented audit trail. Let’s agree to record this information in our version control history alongside each constant definition. Adding a specific field in our commit messages like “Added DISCOUNT_PERCENTAGE_DEFAULT - sourced from marketing strategy” would be a simple and effective way to track the origin.
  8774  +

# Multi-Agent Collaboration Prototype

System uses agents. Agents collaborate. Shared canvas holds work. Adapting for code improvement.

## Features

*   Multi-agent system.
*   Shared canvas.
*   Phase workflow.
*   Structured logging (JSONL).
*   Extensible agents.

## Code Improvement Plan

Based on "Task-Agnostic Code Improvement Plan". Plan guides phases.

## Project Structure

*   `main.py`: Original web design demo.
*   `main_orchestrator.py`: Code improvement workflow. Runs phases.
*   `agents/agent.py`: Agent base class. Defines agent.
*   `agents/canvas.py`: Merges agent work. Updates canvas.
*   `agents/extractors.py`: Gets data from agent output.
*   `agents/logging_utils.py`: Sets up JSONL logs.
*   `files/f-Code Improvement Task Agnostic Plan.md`: The plan document.
*   `sample_code.py`: Example code for agents.

## Setup

Need Python. Need Ollama.
Install deps: `pip install colorama ollama`

## Usage

Run `python main_orchestrator.py`.
Agents process `sample_code.py`.
Output shows progress.
Logs are JSONL.

## Extending

Add agents in `get_agents_for_phase`.
Add phases to list.

## Notes

Prototype state.
Canvas is text.
No file writes yet.

#  Recent 

 Image Prompt:  To visually represent the roles, tasking, reasoning, and thoughts of an AI Tutor as described, you could use the following image prompt: --- **Image Prompt:** **Scene:** A dynamic, multi-layered diagram showing the interactions and processes of an AI Tutor within a learning environment. **Details:** 1. **Interpreter/Executor:** Depict an AI avatar holding a detailed flowchart, representing the breakdown of complex questions into manageable tasks. 2. **Synthesizer/Explainer:** Show the AI avatar with clear, concise diagrams (such as Venn diagrams) and speech bubbles with concise, clear explanations next to it. 3. **Evaluator/Validator:** Illustrate the AI avatar with a progress chart or assessment tool, indicating questions and evaluations being conducted to gauge the learner’s understanding. 4. **Coordinator:** Display a timeline or step-by-step flowchart showing the progress through various stages of learning, with arrows or cues guiding the learner from one step to the next. **Systems Context:** Behind the AI avatar, have a background with interconnected nodes or neural network imagery, symbolizing the vast knowledge base and reasoning engine at work. **Tasking Procedure:** At the bottom or on the sides, show smaller depictions of each stage in the procedure:   - **Receive Input:** A hand dropping a question mark or speech bubble into a “receiving tray” or AI system.   - **Analyze Input:** AI avatar pondering over analysis symbols (such as bubbled thoughts or a magnifying glass over a text).   - **Plan Response:** A thought bubble with varying strategies or plans.   - **Execute Response:** Speech bubbles or diagrams being dispensed to the learner.   - **Monitor Progress:** AI avatar with a progress bar or graph indicating levels of understanding.   - **Iterate:** Cue with an arrow pointing back to the input box, symbolizing continuous feedback and improvement. **Reasoning and Thoughts:**   - **Active Learning:** An active learner (a figurative diagram or simple stick-figure) engaged in a problem, surrounded by question marks and thought bubbles.   - **Scaffolding:** A set of ready-to-hand tools decreasing in size or importance as the learner moves confidently along the task.   - **Personalization:** A personalized learning path with different routes splitting from one starting point, leading to multiple end results representing the learner’s unique progress. **Placebo Pipes:** Depict metaphorical pipes or conduits around the scenario, showing abstract flows of information and helping to visualize the structured and organized nature of tutorials. **Overall Design:** Create the entire scene in a bright, inviting, and visually organized style, kind of like a learning lab or a well-structured classroom diagram, to emphasize clarity and student-centric learning. --- This image prompt would serve as a vivid visual aid to depict the multifaceted roles and processes engaged by an AI Tutor in facilitating learning.

Gemma's Evolution and Accessibility

I've learned that Gemma has rapidly evolved through several versions, including Gemma 1, Gemma 2, and the more recent Gemma 3, along with specialized variants like Gemma 3n and PaliGemma 2. These models are consistently described as 'open models' with 'open weights,' and their code is available on GitHub under an Apache 2.0 license. Access to the models is primarily through Hugging Face and Kaggle, and they operate under a 'Gemma Terms of Use' license that emphasizes responsible AI use. This confirms the open-form nature of the models and their broad accessibility.

Expanding Modalities and Architecture

A significant insight is the expansion of Gemma's capabilities beyond text-only. While the initial Gemma was text-to-text, Gemma 3 and its variants now support multimodal inputs, including text, images, and in some cases, audio and video. PaliGemma 2 is specifically highlighted as a vision-language model. All Gemma models maintain a transformer, decoder-only architecture, with parameter sizes evolving from 2B and 7B in earlier versions to 1B, 4B, 12B, and 27B in Gemma 3. They are trained on diverse datasets, including web data, math, and code.

Addressing Information Gaps and Next Steps

I've identified a need to clarify the precise timeline and features of each Gemma version to create a comprehensive family tree. I also need to find specific details on Gemma's standing on the Open LLM Leaderboard and gather more in-depth technical specifications from model cards on Hugging Face and Kaggle. My next steps will involve browsing the collected URLs to fill these gaps, prioritizing official Google AI blogs and model documentation, and performing a new search for the Open LLM Leaderboard to get the most current performance comparisons.

============ FILE: main_orchestrator.py ============
```python
import logging
import os
from typing import List, Dict, Any

from agent import Agent  # Assuming agent.py is in the same directory
from canvas import Canvas  # Assuming canvas.py is in the same directory
from extractors import extract_system_prompt, extract_updated_canvas  # Assuming extractors.py is in the same directory
from logging_utils import setup_logging  # Assuming logging_utils.py is in the same directory

# Setup structured logging
setup_logging()
logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

# --- Configuration ---
# Define the phases of the code improvement plan
PLAN_PHASES = [
    "Understanding and Assessment",
    "Improvement Implementation",
    "Review and Deployment",
]

# Define the agents and their roles for each phase
# You can customize agents per phase or use a default set
AGENT_ROLES_PER_PHASE: Dict[str, List[Dict[str, str]]] = {
    "Understanding and Assessment": [
        {"name": "ContextGatherer", "persona": "Expert in project documentation and requirements.", "role": "gather context"},
        {"name": "StaticAnalyzer", "persona": "Tool-based code analysis expert.", "role": "perform static analysis"},
        {"name": "CodeReviewer", "persona": "Human-like code quality expert.", "role": "review code readability and maintainability"},
        {"name": "PerformanceProfiler", "persona": "Code performance bottleneck identifier.", "role": "identify performance issues"},
    ],
    "Improvement Implementation": [
        {"name": "Prioritizer", "persona": "Task and problem prioritization expert.", "role": "prioritize identified problems"},
        {"name": "Planner", "persona": "Action plan developer.", "role": "develop implementation plan"},
        {"name": "CodeRestructurer", "persona": "Code organization and modularity expert.", "role": "restructure code"},
        {"name": "CodeRefactorer", "persona": "Code readability and maintainability expert.", "role": "refactor code"},
        {"name": "Documenter", "persona": "Code documentation and commenting expert.", "role": "add documentation and comments"},
        {"name": "LoggerImplementer", "persona": "Logging system expert.", "role": "implement logging"},
        {"name": "TestWriter", "persona": "Unit and integration test expert.", "role": "write tests"},
    ],
    "Review and Deployment": [
        {"name": "CodeReviewApprover", "persona": "Code quality gatekeeper.", "role": "review and approve code changes"},
        {"name": "Deployer", "persona": "Deployment process expert.", "role": "deploy code"},
        {"name": "Monitor", "persona": "Production monitoring expert.", "role": "monitor performance and issues"},
    ],
}

# Default agents if not specified per phase
DEFAULT_AGENTS: List[Dict[str, str]] = [
    {"name": "GeneralAgent", "persona": "A helpful AI assistant.", "role": "assist with the current task"},
]

# Initial prompts (can be refined)
INITIAL_SYSTEM_PROMPT = """You are part of a multi-agent system collaborating on a code improvement task.
Your goal is to contribute to the shared canvas based on your assigned role and the current phase of the project.
Be concise and focus on your specific task within the current phase.
The current phase is: {phase}
Your role in this phase is: {role}
"""

INITIAL_SESSION_PROMPT = """We are working on improving the following code:
{initial_code}

Based on the current phase ({phase}) and your role ({role}), provide your contribution to the canvas.
Remember to be concise and focused.
"""

# --- Main Orchestration Logic ---

def load_code_from_file(filepath: str) -> str:
    """Loads code content from a specified file."""
    try:
        with open(filepath, 'r') as f:
            return f.read()
    except FileNotFoundError:
        logger.error(f"Code file not found: {filepath}")
        return ""
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Error loading code file {filepath}: {e}")
        return ""

def main():
    logger.info("Starting multi-agent code improvement orchestration.")

    # --- Initialize ---
    # Load the initial code to be improved
    code_filepath = "sample_code.py" # <--- Specify your sample code file here
    initial_code = load_code_from_file(code_filepath)
    if not initial_code:
        logger.error("No initial code loaded. Exiting.")
        return

    # Initialize the shared canvas with the initial code
    canvas = Canvas(initial_content=initial_code)
    logger.info("Canvas initialized with initial code.")

    # --- Execute Phases ---
    for phase in PLAN_PHASES:
        logger.info(f"--- Starting Phase: {phase} ---")

        # Get agents for the current phase, or use default agents
        agent_configs = AGENT_ROLES_PER_PHASE.get(phase, DEFAULT_AGENTS)
        agents: List[Agent] = []
        for config in agent_configs:
            # Assuming Agent class takes name, persona, and role
            agents.append(Agent(name=config["name"], persona=config["persona"], role=config["role"]))
        logger.info(f"Initialized {len(agents)} agents for phase: {phase}")

        # Prepare prompts for the current phase
        system_prompt = INITIAL_SYSTEM_PROMPT.format(phase=phase, role="collaborate on the task") # System prompt is general
        # Session prompt includes the initial code and phase/role context for each agent
        session_prompt_template = INITIAL_SESSION_PROMPT

        # Agent Collaboration Loop for the phase
        phase_contributions: List[str] = []
        for agent in agents:
            logger.info(f"Agent {agent.name} ({agent.role}) is contributing to phase: {phase}")
            # Pass the current phase to the agent's generate_response method
            contribution = agent.generate_response(
                system_prompt=system_prompt,
                session_prompt=session_prompt_template.format(initial_code=canvas.get_content(), phase=phase, role=agent.role),
                canvas=canvas.get_content(), # Pass current canvas content
                phase=phase # Pass the current phase
            )
            phase_contributions.append(contribution)
            logger.info(f"Agent {agent.name} contribution received.")

        # Aggregate contributions for the phase
        logger.info(f"Aggregating contributions for phase: {phase}")
        # The Canvas class handles the aggregation logic using an LLM
        canvas.aggregate_contributions(phase_contributions)
        logger.info(f"Canvas updated after phase: {phase}")

        # Optional: Save canvas state after each phase
        # with open(f"canvas_after_{phase.replace(' ', '_').lower()}.md", "w") as f:
        #     f.write(canvas.get_content())
        # logger.info(f"Canvas state saved to canvas_after_{phase.replace(' ', '_').lower()}.md")


    logger.info("--- Orchestration Complete ---")
    logger.info("Final Canvas Content:")
    print(canvas.get_content()) # Print the final result

    # Optional: Save final canvas state
    # with open("final_improved_code.md", "w") as f:
    #     f.write(canvas.get_content())
    # logger.info("Final canvas state saved to final_improved_code.md")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```
